The Forged Letter That Led to Uthman's Murder
Describes the cause of Uthman's murder via a forged letter by Marwan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific cause of Uthman's murder as narrated in classical Sunni sources: the forgery of a letter by Marwan without Uthman's knowledge.

Core Idea
Uthman's murder was instigated by a forged letter, not by his own actions.

This passage from Imam Nasafi's Tabirat al-Adilla recounts the widely accepted Sunni narrative of why Uthman was killed: a letter forged by his relative Marwan, which inflamed the Egyptian rebels. The author presents a clear chain of events, emphasizing Uthman's innocence and Ali's support. Let's examine the details.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Begin by reading the Arabic text once to get a sense of its flow. Then read the English translation to understand the narrative.
The passage is incomplete; the sentence cuts off at the end.
2
Identify the key players
List the main figures: Uthman, Marwan, Ali, Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, Hasan, and Husayn. Notice their roles in the story.
Marwan is the one who forged the letter.
3
Trace the chain of events
Follow the sequence: Uthman appointed a relative over Egypt → people complained → Uthman replaced him with Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr → Marwan forged a letter → the letter was intercepted → Uthman denied it → Ali confirmed Uthman's truthfulness → Ali supported Uthman.
4
Understand the misconception
Some might blame Uthman for his own murder, but this passage shows that the real cause was Marwan's forgery. Uthman was innocent.
The author explicitly states that Uthman was unaware and that Ali testified to his truthfulness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سبب مقتل عثمان : ثم سبب قتله معروف وهو أنه ولى بعض أقاربه مصر فجاء أهل مصر يشكونه إليه فعزله ، وولى محمد بن أبي بكر وبعثه، ثم افتعل مروان كتابا كتبه بيده وختمه بخاتم عثمان لما أنه كان بيده من غير علم لعثمان وأرسله إليه على يد راكب جمل، وظفر به وأنكر الكتاب وقال: فعله مروان، فقال له علي : لقد صدق، فصدقه علي في ذلك وعلم أنه لا يفعل مثل هذا، وكان يعينه وينصره، ولو استغاثه لدفع القوم بالحرب، وكان خرج إلى قرية يوم قتله وأقعد على باب الدار الحسن والحسين يحتطانه ، فلما رجع عاتبهما فقالا: نقب عليه ولم نعلم، ولقد ترك محمد بن أبي بكر قصد قتله والإعانة عليه لما قال له: لو كان أبوك
The cause of Uthman's murder: Then the cause of his killing is known, and that is that he appointed one of his relatives over Egypt. The people of Egypt came complaining to him about him, so he removed him and appointed Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr and sent him. Then Marwan forged a letter, writing it with his own hand and sealing it with Uthman's ring because it was in his possession, without Uthman's knowledge, and sent it to him via a camel rider. It was intercepted, and he (Uthman) denied the letter and said: 'Marwan did it.' So Ali said to him: 'You have spoken the truth.' So Ali affirmed him in that and knew that he would not do such a thing. And he used to support and help him. If he had called for his help, he would have repelled the people with war. And he (Ali) had gone to a village on the day of his killing and seated Hasan and Husayn at the door of the house guarding him. When he returned, he reproached them, and they said: 'It was breached from behind and we did not know.' And indeed Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr abandoned the intention to kill him and the assistance in that when he said to him: 'If your father...'
Source pages p. 1165

Commentary
This passage provides the specific cause of Uthman's murder. The author explains that Uthman appointed a relative (Abdullah ibn Sa'd ibn Abi Sarh) as governor of Egypt. The Egyptians complained, so Uthman replaced him with Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr. However, Marwan, a relative of Uthman, forged a letter in Uthman's name to the former governor, ordering the execution of certain individuals. The letter was intercepted, and Uthman denied it, saying Marwan did it. Ali confirmed Uthman's truthfulness and supported him. The author also mentions that on the day of the murder, Ali was away and left Hasan and Husayn to guard the door, but the attackers broke in from behind. The passage ends with Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr being reminded of his father (Abu Bakr) and consequently abandoning his intent to kill Uthman. This shows that Uthman was innocent of any wrongdoing and that the murder was instigated by Marwan's forgery.

Key Terms
افتعال
مروان
نقب عليه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman was responsible for his own murder due to nepotism and injustice.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the immediate cause was a forged letter by Marwan, not Uthman's policies. Uthman denied the letter, and Ali confirmed his innocence.

Checkpoint
Who forged the letter that led to Uthman's siege?
A) Ali
B) Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr
C) Marwan
D) The Egyptians

Key Takeaway
Uthman's murder was caused by a letter forged by Marwan, not by any wrongdoing of Uthman himself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were Uthman and discovered that someone you trusted (Marwan) forged a letter in your name that led to your death, would you still be able to trust others the same way? What does this teach you about the fragility of reputation and the need for integrity in your own speech and actions?
?
Ali knew the truth, supported Uthman, and tried to protect him, yet he could not prevent the tragedy. Where in your life have you seen truth and right intention fail to stop harm? What does that compel you to do differently today?
?
Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr abandoned his plan to kill Uthman when reminded of his father's legacy. What memory or person stops you from committing a wrong you are considering? Are you actively recalling such reminders, or ignoring them?

Clearing Ali: Uthman's Murder and the Forged Letter
The author narrates Uthman's murder events and clears Ali of involvement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how classical Sunni historians defended Ali from involvement in Uthman's murder and the historical events leading to the caliph's death.

Core Idea
Ali did not kill Uthman; he defended him and prophesied his own martyrdom.

This passage tackles a sensitive historical event—the murder of Caliph Uthman—and addresses accusations against Ali. The author uses Ali's own words and actions to clear him, then narrates the cause of the tragedy, including Marwan's forged letter. By understanding this narrative, you gain insight into Sunni theological positions on the early fitna.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the rhetorical questions and the shift from defense to historical narration.
The author begins with an exclamation to refute an accusation.
2
Examine Ali's denial and interpretation
Focus on the two quotes from Ali: his oath denying involvement and his statement 'Allah killed him and I am with him.' Understand how the author interprets the second statement to clear Ali.
The pronoun 'him' is crucial—it refers to Uthman, not Allah.
3
Trace the cause of Uthman's murder
Identify the sequence: Uthman appointed relatives, complaints arose, he replaced the governor, Marwan forged a letter, and the rebels intercepted it. Notice Ali's role in believing Uthman's denial.
The forgery is a key element in exonerating Uthman of wrongdoing.
4
Observe Ali's support and the guards
Note that Ali supported Uthman, would have fought for him, and that Uthman placed Hasan and Husayn at his door. Also note Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr's restraint.
These details underscore that senior companions opposed the killing.
5
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
Consider how the author uses historical details to build a case that Ali and other prominent Sahaba were not complicit. This shapes Sunni historical memory.
The lesson guards against a sectarian misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يستعين بعلي ؟! وكيف يستنصر من هو جاد في نصره مشمر ذيله في ذلك؟! وروى عنه له أنه قال : - والله ما قتلت عثمان ولا مالات في قتله - وما روي عن علي ه أنه قال في أمر عثمان: الله قتله وأنا معه - معناه: وأنا مع عثمان وكانت - الهاء عائدة إلى عثمان دون الله تعالى، وأخبر أنه يستشهد كما استشهد عثمان رضي الله عنهما. يحققه أنه قال على المنبر : - قتلت يوم قتل الثور الأبيض - وهو مثل مشهور في العرب، أخبر بذلك أنه يستشهد كما استشهد هو، والله الموفق. سبب مقتل عثمان : ثم سبب قتله معروف وهو أنه كان ولى بعض أقاربه مصر فجاء أهل مصر يشكونه إليه فعزله، وولى محمد بن أبي بكر وبعثه، ثم افتعل مروان كتابا كتبه بيده وختمه بخاتم عثمان لما أنه كان بيده من غير علم لعثمان وأرسله إليه على يد راكب جمل، وظُفر به وأنكر الكتاب وقال: فعله مروان، فقال له علي ه: لقد صدق، فصدقه علي في ذلك وعلم أنه لا يفعل مثل هذا، وكان يعينه وينصره، ولو استغاثه لدفع القوم بالحرب، وكان خرج إلى قرية يوم قتله وأقعد على باب الدار الحسن والحسين يحتطانه، فلما رجع عاتبهما فقالا: نُقبَ عليه ولم نعلم، ولقد ترك محمد بن أبي بكر قصد قتله والإعانة عليه لما قال له: لو كان أبوك في الأحياء لاستحييت منه - أو كما قال، فانصرف ثانيًا عنه
Does he seek help from Ali?! And how can he seek victory from one who was serious in supporting him, having rolled up his sleeves for that? And it was narrated from him that he said: 'By Allah, I did not kill Uthman nor did I assist in his killing.' And what was narrated from Ali (رضي الله عنه) that he said regarding the matter of Uthman: 'Allah killed him and I am with him'—its meaning: 'I am with Uthman' and the pronoun refers to Uthman, not Allah. And he informed that he would be martyred just as Uthman was martyred, may Allah be pleased with them both. He confirmed it by saying on the pulpit: 'I was killed on the day the white bull was killed'—and this is a famous proverb among the Arabs; by that he informed that he would be martyred just as he (Uthman) was martyred. And Allah is the Grantor of success. The reason for the murder of Uthman: Then the cause of his killing is known: he appointed some of his relatives over Egypt, so the people of Egypt came complaining against him to him, so he removed him and appointed Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr and sent him. Then Marwan forged a letter written in his own hand sealed with Uthman's seal, since it was in his possession without Uthman's knowledge, and sent it to him (the governor) via a camel rider. It was intercepted, and he (Uthman) denied the letter and said: 'Marwan did it.' So Ali (رضي الله عنه) said to him: 'He spoke the truth.' So Ali believed him in that and knew that he would not do such a thing. And he (Ali) was helping and supporting him (Uthman); had he (Uthman) sought his aid, he would have repelled the people with war. And he (Uthman) had gone out to a village on the day of his murder and seated al-Hasan and al-Husayn at the door of the house to guard him. When he returned, he reproached them, and they said: 'They broke in upon him and we did not know.' And indeed Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr abandoned the intention to kill him and to assist in it, when he said to him: 'If your father were alive, I would have been ashamed before him'—or as he said. So he turned away from him a second time.
Source pages p. 1165

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative and theological defense. The author begins by addressing an accusation that Ali (رضي الله عنه) was complicit in Uthman's killing. He quotes Ali's oath denying involvement and interprets his enigmatic statement 'Allah killed him and I am with him' to mean 'I am with Uthman,' not that he approved the killing. Ali also prophesied his own martyrdom through a proverb. Then the author narrates the cause: Uthman appointed relatives, leading to complaints. He appointed Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, but Marwan forged a letter that incited the rebels. Ali defended Uthman and believed his denial. Uthman stationed Hasan and Husayn to guard him. Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr refrained from killing out of respect for his father. Thus the author shows that senior companions did not support the killing.

Key Terms
قتل
شهادة
كتاب مفتعل
تبرئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ali (رضي الله عنه) was complicit in the killing of Uthman (رضي الله عنه).
Correction: The text shows Ali denied involvement, interpreted his own words to mean he was with Uthman, supported Uthman, and even prophesied his own martyrdom like Uthman.

Checkpoint
What did Ali (رضي الله عنه) say about his involvement in Uthman's death according to the text?
A) He was involved in the killing.
B) He denied involvement, saying he neither killed nor assisted.
C) He remained silent on the matter.
D) He ordered the killing.

Key Takeaway
The passage defends Ali by presenting his own denials, prophetic statements, and actions showing his loyalty to Uthman, all within a historical narrative of the murder.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone you love is falsely accused, do you stand by them with the same conviction that Ali showed for Uthman? What fears or doubts hold you back from defending them wholeheartedly? Write one specific step you will take to be a protector of the truth for those who are wronged.
?
The forgery by Marwan changed history and led to immense fitna. Think of a time you heard a rumor or accusation about someone. Did you investigate it before accepting or passing it on? What will you do differently from now on to ensure your words do not forge injustice against another soul?
?
Ali's prophecy about his own death shows his certainty in Allah's decree. Are you attached to the outcomes of this world to the point that you would compromise truth? What is one worldly attachment that prevents you from submitting fully to Allah's plan, and how will you strive to detach from it today?

The Events of Uthman's Unjust Murder
Description of the unjust killing of Uthman and his virtuous conduct.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific events surrounding Uthman's murder and how they demonstrate his innocence.

Core Idea
Uthman's murder was unjust: he was fasting, recited Quran, and refused to shed Muslim blood.

The author begins by describing the circumstances of Uthman's killing, painting a vivid picture of his piety and restraint. This narrative sets the stage for the later argument about the silence of the senior companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative passage
Read the Arabic passage describing the murder and its circumstances. Notice the details provided: the killer, the dream, the fasting, and Uthman's statement.
The text uses strong language: 'killed him unjustly'.
2
Identify Uthman's virtues
Look for actions that show Uthman's piety: reciting Quran, seeing the Prophet in a dream, fasting, relying on Allah, and avoiding bloodshed.
3
Understand the dream and fasting
The dream from the Prophet instructs Uthman to break his fast with him, indicating his impending death. Uthman began fasting that day, awaiting the decree.
This shows his acceptance of fate.
4
Reflect on his refusal to shed blood
Uthman refused to allow his supporters to fight the attackers, saying he did not want a drop of Muslim blood shed for his sake. This demonstrates his mercy and selflessness.
Contrast this with the killers' aggression.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أقدم عليه من لا له في فضل ولا يعد من العلماء ولا من الفضلاء، فقتله ظلما وهو يقرأ من سورة فسيكفيكهم الله وهو السميع العليم، وكان رأى النبي عليه السلام في منامه بارحة ذلك اليوم أنه قال: لا تفطر حتى تفطر معي فأصبح صائمًا منتظرا القضاء دافعا عن نفسه الردى بالتحصن بالدار متوكلاً على الله في أمره مفوضا أمره إليه متحرزاً عن إراقة دماء المسلمين حتى قال: لا أريد أن يراق في ولايتي قدر محجم من دم مسلم حين طلب منه الإذن فيه ليدفعوا الغوغاء والسفلة عنه. ثم الدليل على أنه قتل مظلومًا، وأنه لم يكن مستحقا للقتل والخلع أن كبار الصحابة ومن بقي من المبشرين بالجنة ومن أهل الشورى والبدريين والمهاجرين الأولين والأنصار - رضوان الله عليهم أجمعين لم يشتغلوا بخلعه ولا أرادوا نزعه ولا حاربوه ولا لاموه على فعل من الأفعال وأمر من الأمور، ولو كان الله استحق ذلك لكان أولى به كبار الصحابة ومن سميناهم لا شذاذ القبائل والغوغاء من الخلق والجهال من الناس الذين لم يكن لهم في العلم نصيب ولا مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صحبة، أفترى أن عليّا وطلحة والزبير ومن سواهم من أفاضل الصحابة وعلمائهم وكبار خليقة الله تعالى وخيار البشر كانوا يرون المناكير من عثمان
Then came upon him one who has no merit nor is counted among the scholars or the virtuous, and he killed him unjustly while he was reciting from the surah: 'So Allah will suffice you against them, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Knowing' (Qur'an 2:137). And he (Uthman) had seen the Prophet (peace be upon him) in a dream the night before that day, saying: 'Do not break your fast until you break it with me.' So he woke up fasting, awaiting the decree, repelling ruin from himself by fortifying himself in the house, relying on Allah in his affair, entrusting his affair to Him, cautious about shedding the blood of Muslims, until he said: 'I do not want that during my caliphate a single cupping-glass of Muslim blood should be shed' when he was asked for permission to repel the rabble and the lowly from him. Then the evidence that he was killed unjustly and that he was not deserving of killing or removal is that the senior Companions, those who remained of the ten promised Paradise, the people of the shura (council), the Badriyyun (participants of Badr), the early Muhajirun and Ansar—may Allah be pleased with them all—did not engage in removing him, nor did they desire his removal, nor did they fight him, nor did they blame him for any of his actions or matters. If he had deserved that (removal), then the senior Companions and those we have named would have been worthier of it, not the riffraff of the tribes, the rabble, the ignorant people who have no share in knowledge nor companionship with the Prophet (peace be upon him). Do you think that Ali, Talhah, al-Zubayr, and others among the virtuous Companions and their scholars, the great ones of Allah's creation and the best of mankind, would have seen disapproved things from Uthman...
Source pages p. 1166

Commentary
This passage is a proof of Uthman's unjust murder. The author describes the killer as lacking virtue and merit. Uthman was killed while reciting the Quran and fasting after a dream from the Prophet. He refused to allow bloodshed in his defense, showing his restraint. Then the author presents the main argument: the senior Sahaba—including the ten promised Paradise, the people of the shura, Badriyyun, Muhajirun, and Ansar—did not attempt to remove Uthman or blame him. If he had deserved removal, they would have acted, not the ignorant rabble. The rhetorical question implies that these virtuous Companions would not have tolerated evil from Uthman if it existed, but they remained silent, proving his innocence. Thus, the killers were outsiders and ignoramuses.

Key Terms
قتل مظلوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman was a tyrant who deserved removal.
Correction: The text shows he was a pious man who refused to use force against Muslims, even to save his own life.

Checkpoint
What did Uthman say when asked for permission to repel the attackers?
A) 'Fight them with all your might.'
B) 'I do not want a single cupping-glass of Muslim blood shed.'
C) 'Let them kill me, I am ready.'
D) 'I will surrender to them.'

Key Takeaway
Uthman's conduct during the siege proves his innocence and unjust murder.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are wronged or under pressure, do you trust Allah like Uthman did, or do you try to fight back for your rights? What would you sacrifice to avoid shedding blood—whether literal or figurative?
?
Uthman obeyed the Prophet's command from a dream immediately and without question. How attentive are you to divine guidance in your life? Are you willing to change your plans based on a sign or inner conviction, no matter the cost?
?
Uthman refused to let his supporters shed Muslim blood to save his own life. Is your love for your community strong enough to sacrifice your own safety, reputation, or comfort for its unity? What does your answer reveal about your faith?

The Proof from the Senior Companions' Silence
Proof that Uthman was killed unjustly based on senior companions' lack of opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the silence of the senior companions serves as evidence for Uthman's innocence.

Core Idea
If Uthman deserved removal, the senior companions would have acted; their silence proves his innocence.

After describing the murder, the author presents a rational proof: the most virtuous companions did not oppose Uthman or seek his removal. This silence indicates that he was not deserving of punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof passage
Read the Arabic passage beginning with 'Then the evidence that he was killed unjustly...'. Notice the list of groups mentioned.
2
Identify the groups of senior companions
The author enumerates several categories: the ten promised Paradise, the shura council, Badriyyun, early Muhajirun, and Ansar. Recognize that these are the most respected and knowledgeable companions.
3
Understand the argument from silence
The author argues that these senior companions did not attempt to remove Uthman, fight him, or even blame him. Their inaction proves he was not deserving of removal, because if he were, they would have been the first to act.
4
Reflect on the rhetorical question
The passage ends with a rhetorical question: would Ali, Talhah, al-Zubayr and others have tolerated evil from Uthman? The implied answer is no, so Uthman must have been innocent.
This question reinforces the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أقدم عليه من لا له في فضل ولا يعد من العلماء ولا من الفضلاء، فقتله ظلما وهو يقرأ من سورة فسيكفيكهم الله وهو السميع العليم، وكان رأى النبي عليه السلام في منامه بارحة ذلك اليوم أنه قال: لا تفطر حتى تفطر معي فأصبح صائمًا منتظرا القضاء دافعا عن نفسه الردى بالتحصن بالدار متوكلاً على الله في أمره مفوضا أمره إليه متحرزاً عن إراقة دماء المسلمين حتى قال: لا أريد أن يراق في ولايتي قدر محجم من دم مسلم حين طلب منه الإذن فيه ليدفعوا الغوغاء والسفلة عنه. ثم الدليل على أنه قتل مظلومًا، وأنه لم يكن مستحقا للقتل والخلع أن كبار الصحابة ومن بقي من المبشرين بالجنة ومن أهل الشورى والبدريين والمهاجرين الأولين والأنصار - رضوان الله عليهم أجمعين لم يشتغلوا بخلعه ولا أرادوا نزعه ولا حاربوه ولا لاموه على فعل من الأفعال وأمر من الأمور، ولو كان الله استحق ذلك لكان أولى به كبار الصحابة ومن سميناهم لا شذاذ القبائل والغوغاء من الخلق والجهال من الناس الذين لم يكن لهم في العلم نصيب ولا مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صحبة، أفترى أن عليّا وطلحة والزبير ومن سواهم من أفاضل الصحابة وعلمائهم وكبار خليقة الله تعالى وخيار البشر كانوا يرون المناكير من عثمان
Then came upon him one who has no merit nor is counted among the scholars or the virtuous, and he killed him unjustly while he was reciting from the surah: 'So Allah will suffice you against them, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Knowing' (Qur'an 2:137). And he (Uthman) had seen the Prophet (peace be upon him) in a dream the night before that day, saying: 'Do not break your fast until you break it with me.' So he woke up fasting, awaiting the decree, repelling ruin from himself by fortifying himself in the house, relying on Allah in his affair, entrusting his affair to Him, cautious about shedding the blood of Muslims, until he said: 'I do not want that during my caliphate a single cupping-glass of Muslim blood should be shed' when he was asked for permission to repel the rabble and the lowly from him. Then the evidence that he was killed unjustly and that he was not deserving of killing or removal is that the senior Companions, those who remained of the ten promised Paradise, the people of the shura (council), the Badriyyun (participants of Badr), the early Muhajirun and Ansar—may Allah be pleased with them all—did not engage in removing him, nor did they desire his removal, nor did they fight him, nor did they blame him for any of his actions or matters. If he had deserved that (removal), then the senior Companions and those we have named would have been worthier of it, not the riffraff of the tribes, the rabble, the ignorant people who have no share in knowledge nor companionship with the Prophet (peace be upon him). Do you think that Ali, Talhah, al-Zubayr, and others among the virtuous Companions and their scholars, the great ones of Allah's creation and the best of mankind, would have seen disapproved things from Uthman...
Source pages p. 1166

Commentary
This passage is a proof of Uthman's unjust murder. The author describes the killer as lacking virtue and merit. Uthman was killed while reciting the Quran and fasting after a dream from the Prophet. He refused to allow bloodshed in his defense, showing his restraint. Then the author presents the main argument: the senior Sahaba—including the ten promised Paradise, the people of the shura, Badriyyun, Muhajirun, and Ansar—did not attempt to remove Uthman or blame him. If he had deserved removal, they would have acted, not the ignorant rabble. The rhetorical question implies that these virtuous Companions would not have tolerated evil from Uthman if it existed, but they remained silent, proving his innocence. Thus, the killers were outsiders and ignoramuses.

Key Terms
إجماع الصحابة
الشورى
المبشرون بالجنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author use as the main evidence that Uthman was killed unjustly?
A) The killers were ignorant and without merit.
B) The senior companions did not oppose Uthman or seek his removal.
C) Uthman was a relative of the Prophet.
D) Uthman was killed while praying.

Key Takeaway
The silence of the virtuous companions is the strongest proof that Uthman was unjustly killed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear criticism of a believer, do you pause to ask: 'Would the most righteous among us agree with this criticism?' The senior Companions' silence was proof of Uthman's innocence. How often do you add your voice to condemnation without first checking if those with deeper knowledge and virtue would remain silent?
?
The rhetorical question in this passage challenges you directly: 'Do you think that Ali, Talhah, al-Zubayr and the best of creation would have seen disapproved things from Uthman?' Now apply that to your own judgments: when you spot a fault in a fellow Muslim, are you quick to assume the worst, or do you give them the benefit of the doubt as the Companions did for Uthman? What would change in your relationships if you adopted this principle?
?
This lesson teaches that the ignorant rabble—not the learned and virtuous—were the ones who acted against Uthman. In your own life, when you are tempted to take a stand against someone, ask yourself: Am I acting from knowledge and virtue, or from ignorance and mob mentality? How can you ensure you are not among those who 'have no share in knowledge'?

Uthman's Conduct on the Day of His Martyrdom
Narrative of Uthman's dream, fasting, and fortification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the narrative of Uthman's final day, including his dream, his fasting, and his refusal to shed Muslim blood, which demonstrates his innocence and piety.

Core Idea
Uthman's dream, fasting, and restraint prove his innocence even at the moment of death.

Al-Nasafi opens his proof that Uthman was killed unjustly by describing the events of his final day. The narrative shows Uthman's piety and his reluctance to shed blood, establishing his righteousness before the argument from consensus is presented.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the sequence of events: the assassin, the dream, the fasting, the fortification, and the refusal to fight.
The narrative is rich in detail—pay attention to Uthman's state of mind.
2
Identify key actions of Uthman
List the actions Uthman took on his final day: seeing the dream, fasting, fortifying himself, trusting in Allah, and refusing to shed Muslim blood.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider how these actions portray Uthman as a pious and innocent leader. How does this set the stage for the main argument that he was killed unjustly?
This narrative counteracts any suggestion that Uthman deserved death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في الأحياء لاستحييت منه - أو كما قال، فانصرف ثانيًا عنه، ثم أقدم عليه من لا له في فضل ولا يعد من العلماء ولا من الفضلاء، فقتله ظلما وهو يقرأ من سورة فَسَيَكْفِيكَهُمُ اللَّهُ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْعَلِيمُ وكان رأى النبي عليه السلام في منامه بارحة ذلك اليوم أنه قال: لا تفطر حتى تفطر معي فأصبح صائمًا منتظرا القضاء دافعا عن نفسه الردى بالتحصن بالدار متوكلاً على الله في أمره مفوضا أمره إليه متحرزاً عن إراقة دماء المسلمين حتى قال: لا أريد أن يراق في ولايتي قدر مِحْجَمٍ من دم مسلم حين طلب منه الإذن فيه ليدفعوا الغوغاء والسفلة عنه. ثم الدليل على أنه قتل مظلومًا، وأنه لم يكن مستحقا للقتل والخلع أن كبار الصحابة ومن بقي من المبشرين بالجنة ومن أهل الشورى والبدريين والمهاجرين الأولين والأنصار - رضوان الله عليهم أجمعين لم يشتغلوا بخلعه ولا أرادوا نزعه ولا حاربوه ولا لاموه على فعل من الأفعال وأمر من الأمور، ولو كان الله استحق ذلك لكان أولى به كبار الصحابة ومن سميناهم لا شذاذ القبائل والغوغاء من الخلق والجهال من الناس الذين لم يكن لهم في العلم نصيب ولا مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صحبة، أفترى أن عليّا وطلحة والزبير ومن سواهم من أفاضل الصحابة وعلمائهم وكبار خليقة الله تعالى وخيار البشر كانوا يرون المناكير من عثمان وكان يغمضون عنها ويمتنعون عن تغييرها والأمر بما يضادها من المعروف، ويرضون بإمامة من هو مستحق للخلع غير صالح للإمامة، وينقادون لأوامره ونواهيه ولا يتعرضون له في إقامة الصلوات والتحكم في الأموال والدماء والفروج، وبسط اليد في أموال بيت المسلمين وهم يعتقدون أنه غير محق فيما يفعل بل هو ظالم متعد حتى جاء من أهل مصر وأهل العراق من لا سابقة له في الإسلام ولا علم له بشيء من أمور الدين، فغيروا كل منكر وأزالوا عن الإسلام معرة الظالم الجائر المبطل، وأراحوا كبار الصحابة عن شره، وتداركوا ما ضيعه المهاجرون والأنصار من حقوق الدين، وقاموا بنصرة من خذله أولئك من المظلومين وحافظوا ما أهمله أولئك من حدود الشرع؟!!. هذا، والله المحال الظاهر والخطأ البين، ووصف خيار الخلق بغير ما وصفهم الله تعالى به وبالوقوف على هذه الجملة يظهر أن بغي جميع الروافض يؤول إلى إلحاق شين ونقص بعلي الله والحمد لله الذي عصمنا عن الطعن في خيرة خليقته ونجباء بريته المكرمين بصحبة نبيه، الموفقين للقيام بنصرة ما ارتضاه من الدين لعباده الباذلين مهجهم وأموالهم في ذات الله تعالى.
In the living beings, I would have been ashamed of him - or as he said, so he turned away from him a second time, then someone who has no merit and is not counted among the scholars or the virtuous advanced against him and killed him unjustly while he was reciting from the surah: 'So Allah will suffice you against them, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Knowing.' And he had seen the Prophet, peace be upon him, in his dream the night before that day saying: 'Do not break your fast until you break it with me.' So he began the day fasting, awaiting the decree, repelling destruction from himself by fortifying himself in the house, trusting in Allah in his affair, delegating his affair to Him, guarding against the shedding of Muslim blood, until he said: 'I do not want in my governorship even the amount of a cupping glass of a Muslim's blood to be shed,' when he was asked for permission to fight back the mob and rabble. Then the proof that he was killed unjustly and that he did not deserve killing or deposition is that the senior Companions, those who remained of the ones given glad tidings of Paradise, the people of the Shura, the Badr participants, the first Muhajirun, and the Ansar - may Allah be pleased with them all - did not engage in deposing him, nor did they desire to remove him, nor did they fight him, nor did they blame him for any action or matter. And if he had deserved that, then it would have been more appropriate for the senior Companions and those we named, not the riffraff of the tribes, the mob of creation, and the ignorant people who have no share in knowledge and no companionship with the Prophet, peace be upon him. Do you think that Ali, Talha, al-Zubayr, and others among the virtuous Companions, their scholars, the great creatures of Allah Almighty, and the best of mankind saw reprehensible acts from Uthman and winked at them, refrained from changing them and commanding what opposes them of good, and were satisfied with the imamate of one who deserves deposition and is not fit for imamate, and submitted to his commands and prohibitions without confronting him regarding the establishment of prayers, the control of wealth, blood, and private parts, and the extension of the hand over the wealth of the Muslims' treasury, while they believed that he was not right in what he did but rather was an oppressor and transgressor, until those from Egypt and Iraq who had no precedence in Islam and no knowledge of any matters of religion came and changed every reprehensible act, removed from Islam the shame of the unjust, oppressive, and false, gave the senior Companions relief from his evil, compensated for what the Muhajirun and Ansar had neglected of the rights of religion, supported those whom those had failed of the oppressed, and preserved what those had neglected of the limits of the Sharia?!! This, by Allah, is clear absurdity and manifest error. Describing the best of creation other than what Allah Almighty described them, and upon considering this statement, it becomes clear that the transgression of all the Rafidah leads to attaching defect and deficiency to 'Aliyy. And praise be to Allah who protected us from attacking the best of His creation and the nobles of His creatures, honored by the companionship of His Prophet, successful in undertaking to support what He chose of the religion for His servants, sacrificing their lives and wealth for the sake of Allah Almighty.
Source pages p. 1166

Commentary
This passage is a proof that Uthman ibn Affan was killed unjustly, presented by Imam al-Nasafi in the context of a sectarian discussion refuting the Rafidah (extreme Shi'a) claims. The passage begins with a narrative: Uthman, on the day of his assassination, had seen the Prophet in a dream telling him not to break his fast until he breaks it with him. Uthman thus began the day fasting, awaiting his fate, fortifying himself in his house, refraining from shedding Muslim blood, even refusing permission to fight off the mob. Then the author presents the main proof: the senior Companions—those promised Paradise, the members of the Shura council, the participants of Badr, the early Muhajirun and Ansar—did not attempt to depose Uthman, nor did they fight him or blame him for any deed. If Uthman had truly deserved deposition or execution, it would have been the senior Companions, not the ignorant rabble, who would have carried it out. The author then asks a rhetorical question: Could it be that Ali, Talha, al-Zubayr, and other virtuous Companions saw wrongdoing from Uthman and remained silent, acquiescing to an unjust imam, while believing he was an oppressor? That would be absurd. The author argues that it was only later, when people from Egypt and Iraq with no Islamic precedence or knowledge came, that they claimed to remove evil, accusing the senior Companions of neglecting their duty. The author concludes that this is clear error and that such accusations actually defame the best of creation, implying defect even toward Ali. The praise of Allah for protecting the author from attacking the Companions ends the passage. The argument relies on the consensus (ijma') of the senior Sahaba in not opposing Uthman, taken as evidence of his rightful imamate and the injustice of his killing.

ظلما
صائمًا
التحصن بالدار
متحرزاً

Key Takeaway
Uthman's actions on his final day demonstrate his innocence and piety, refuting claims that he deserved death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Uthman trusted Allah completely even as death approached. In what area of your life are you holding back from surrendering control to Allah, and what is one step you can take today to truly rely on Him?
?
Uthman refused to allow even a cupping-glass of Muslim blood to be shed for his sake. Are there relationships or conflicts in your life where you are willing to harm others (even subtly) to defend your own honor or rights? Will you commit today to prioritize peace over pride?
?
Uthman's dream of the Prophet prepared him for his martyrdom. If you knew you had only one day left, what would you change about how you spend your time, and are you ready to meet your Lord right now?

The Proof of Uthman's Rightful Imamate from the Senior Companions' Silence
Proof from the senior Companions' consensus on Uthman's imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Nasafi's argument that the inaction of senior Companions in deposing Uthman proves he was killed unjustly and was a rightful imam.

Core Idea
If Uthman had been unjust, the senior Companions would have removed him—their silence proves his innocence.

After narrating Uthman's conduct, Al-Nasafi presents his main proof: the senior Companions, including Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr, never attempted to depose Uthman. This consensus of the elite Sahaba demonstrates that Uthman was not deserving of deposition or death. Al-Nasafi then uses a rhetorical question to expose the absurdity of the contrary claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the list of Companions mentioned and the structure of the argument.
The passage is dense with rhetorical force.
2
Identify the groups of Companions
List the groups: senior Companions, those promised Paradise, Shura members, Badr participants, early Muhajirun, and Ansar.
These are the highest authorities in the early Muslim community.
3
Understand the rhetorical question
Al-Nasafi asks rhetorically whether these Companions would have remained silent if Uthman were truly unjust. This highlights the absurdity of the claim.
The question implies that the Companions are incapable of such negligence.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that accusing the Companions of negligence actually defames Ali and the best of creation.
This ties the argument to refuting Rafidah claims.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the silence of senior Companions on Uthman's actions implies they approved of wrongdoing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Do you truly believe that the Companions were incapable of failing in this duty? Examine your own allegiance to the Sahaba: do you view them as perfect or as human leaders worthy of respect? How does your view affect your relationship with Islamic history?
?
Are you willing to accept the logical conclusion that accusing Uthman of injustice actually implies accusing Ali and the other senior Companions of negligence? How does that strike your conscience? Will you let that implication change how you speak about the early caliphs?

Refutation of the Rafidite Slander Against the Companions
The author refutes the Rafidite claim that the Companions failed in their duties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the Rafidite claim that the Companions failed in their duties, using sarcasm and theological reasoning.

Core Idea
The Rafidite narrative about the Companions is manifest absurdity, contradicting Allah's praise.

The author addresses a serious calumny: the Rafidite accusation that the Companions of the Prophet were complicit in injustice and neglected their duties. He presents their claim in a sarcastic tone, then declares it absurd by pointing to the Quranic praise of the Companions. This lesson examines the author's refutation and his defense of the Sahaba's honor.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the sarcastic tone in the first part.
2
Identify the two parts
The first part presents the Rafidite claim (sarcastically), the second part refutes it.
3
Understand the refutation argument
The author calls it 'manifest absurdity' and points out that it contradicts Allah's description of the Companions.
4
Recognize the deeper implication
The Rafidite attack on the Companions ultimately aims to attach defect to Ali (RA).
5
Reflect on the author's gratitude
He thanks Allah for protection from such slander.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكان يغمضون عنها ويمتنعون عن تغييرها والأمر بما يضادها من المعروف، ويرضون بإمامة من هو مستحق للخلع غير صالح للإمامة، وينقادون لأوامره ونواهيه ولا يتعرضون له في إقامة الصلوات والتحكم في الأموال والدماء والفروج، وبسط اليد في أموال بيت المسلمين وهم يعتقدون أنه غير محق فيما يفعل بل هو ظالم متعد حتى جاء من أهل مصر وأهل العراق من لا سابقة له في الإسلام ولا علم له بشيء من أمور الدين، فغيروا كل منكر وأزالوا عن الإسلام معرة الظالم الجائر المبطل، وأراحوا كبار الصحابة عن شره، وتداركوا ما ضيعه المهاجرون والأنصار من حقوق الدين، وقاموا بنصرة من خذله أولئك من المظلومين وحافظوا ما أهمله أولئك من حدود الشرع؟!!. هذا، والله المحال الظاهر والخطأ البين، ووصف خيار الخلق بغير ما وصفهم الله تعالى به وبالوقوف على هذه الجملة يظهر أن بغي جميع الروافض يؤول إلى إلحاق شين ونقص بعلي الله والحمد لله الذي عصمنا عن الطعن في خيرة خليقته ونجباء بريته المكرمين بصحبة نبيه، الموفقين للقيام بنصرة ما ارتضاه من الدين لعباده الباذلين مهجهم وأموالهم في ذات الله تعالى.
And they (the Rafidites) were closing their eyes to it and refraining from changing it and commanding what opposes it from the good, and they were content with the leadership of one who deserves to be removed, unfit for leadership, and they obeyed his commands and prohibitions and did not oppose him in establishing prayers and controlling wealth, blood, and private parts, and extending his hand over the wealth of the Muslims while believing that he is not right in what he does but rather is an oppressor and transgressor, until there came from the people of Egypt and the people of Iraq those who had no precedence in Islam nor knowledge of anything of the affairs of religion, so they changed every wrong and removed from Islam the disgrace of the oppressive, unjust, false ruler, and gave relief to the senior Companions from his evil, and rectified what the Emigrants and Helpers neglected of the rights of religion, and stood in support of the oppressed whom those (Companions) had abandoned, and preserved what those (Companions) had neglected of the limits of the Sharia?! This, by Allah, is manifest absurdity and clear error, and describing the best of creation with other than what Allah described them with, and by pausing at this summary it appears that the transgression of all the Rafidites leads to attaching defect and deficiency to 'Ali, and praise be to Allah who protected us from attacking the best of His creation and the nobles of His creatures honored by the companionship of His Prophet, those who were guided to stand in support of what He has approved of the religion for His servants, donating their lives and wealth for the sake of Allah.
Source pages p. 1167

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Rafidite (Rawafid) claims against the Companions of the Prophet (Sahaba). The author begins by presenting the Rafidite accusation: that the Companions willingly allowed an unworthy leader (referring to the caliphs before 'Ali) to rule, obeying his unjust commands and not opposing him. The Rafidites claim that the Companions were silent about oppression and even pleased with it. Then the author sarcastically says that it was only when some ignorant people from Egypt and Iraq came (referring to the rebels who killed 'Uthman) that they 'corrected' the situation and removed the 'disgrace.' The use of the question mark and exclamation indicates that the author is quoting the Rafidite narrative in a mocking tone. Then he declares that this narrative is manifest absurdity and clear error. He points out that describing the best of creation (the Sahaba) in such a way is contrary to what Allah has said about them. The Rafidites' claim ultimately aims to attach defect to 'Ali by association. The author ends by praising Allah for protecting him from such slander.

الصحابة
الخلع
الإمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is presenting his own view when he sarcastically describes the Rafidite narrative.
Correction: Actually, the author is using sarcasm to depict the Rafidite claim before refuting it. His own view is that the narrative is absurd.

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the author's attitude towards the Rafidite claim presented in the passage?
A) He agrees with it.
B) He refutes it as absurd.
C) He is neutral.
D) He praises the Rafidites.

Key Takeaway
The Rafidite claim against the Companions is not only false but also blasphemous, as it contradicts Allah's praise and ultimately defames Ali.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author calls the Rafidite narrative 'manifest absurdity.' Are there any popular narratives about the early Muslims that you have accepted without checking against the Qur'an and authentic Sunnah? What will you do to verify them starting now?
?
The author thanks Allah for protection from attacking the Companions. Do you feel that same gratitude? If not, what belief or attitude in your heart needs to change so that you stand firmly with the Sahaba as Allah described them?

Proof of 'Ali's excellence and the legitimacy of his caliphate
The author demonstrates 'Ali's qualities and describes how the caliphate was offered to him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses 'Ali's personal virtues and the historical events following 'Uthman's murder to argue for the legitimacy of his caliphate.

Core Idea
'Ali's caliphate was both by merit and by the consent of the senior Companions.

This passage from Tabsirat al-Adilla presents a theological and historical argument for 'Ali's imamate. The author first enumerates 'Ali's unparalleled virtues, then describes how the caliphate was offered to him by the senior Companions after 'Uthman's murder, despite his initial reluctance. Understanding this argument is crucial for Maturidi perspectives on the caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the flow: first virtues, then a quote from 'Ali, then the events after 'Uthman's murder.
2
Identify the list of virtues
Locate the specific qualities the author attributes to 'Ali: lineage, upbringing by the Prophet, marriage to Fatima, knowledge, asceticism, piety, courage, military skill.
These are presented as well-known and undeniable.
3
Focus on 'Ali's own quote
Read 'Ali's statement denying Quraysh's claim that he lacks war experience. Note how he emphasizes his long experience and his frustration with being disobeyed.
4
Understand the historical context
Identify the murderers of 'Uthman and their demand for a caliph. See how the Companions offered the caliphate to 'Ali to prevent sedition, and 'Ali's initial refusal.
5
Summarize the overall argument
Reflect on how the author combines personal excellence and historical necessity to prove 'Ali's right to the caliphate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في إمامة علي بن أبي طالب: نقول : إن عليا ممن لا يخفى على أحد نسبه واختصاصه برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وتربيته إياه وتزويجه كريمته فاطمة الزهراء - رضي الله عنها — منه ولا علمه ولا زهده ولا ورعه، فأما شجاعته وبأسه ونجدته وعلمه بتدبير الجيوش وجر العساكر وبصارته بمكائد الحرب وحماية البيضة مما صار هو به مثلاً سائرا تتداوله الألسن وتعتقده الأفئدة، والرواية عنه مشهورة أنه قال: إن قريشًا تقول إن ابن أبي طالب رجل شجاع، ولكن لا رأي له في الحرب، الله أمرهم من ذا يكون أبصر بها مني وأشد لها مراسًا، والله لقد نهضت فيها وما بلغت العشرين، وها أنا اليوم وقد أشرفت على الستين، ولكن لا أمرة لمن لا يطاع - وهذا أوضح من أن يشتغل بإثباته، ومن ارتاب في أمر من هذه الأمور فهو الأحمق الذي لا دواء لحمقه. ثم بعد ثبوت هذه الشرائط فقد عقدت له الخلافة وهو يومئذ أفضل خليقة الله تعالى على وجه الأرض وأولاهم بها، ثم المتولي لعقدها له كبار الصحابة وأئمة الخلق وخيار من بقي من الصحابة، فإن من المشهور أن قتلة عثمان له كالغافقي وكتانة بن بشر النجيبي، وسوار بن حمران وعبد الله بن شديد بن ورقاء و عمرو بن الحمق الخزاعيين، وآخرين منهم لما قتلوه قصدوا الاستيلاء على المدينة وهموا بالفتك بأهلها وحلفوا على ذلك للصحابة متى لم يقدموا للنظر في أمرهم ويعقدوا الإمامة لرجل منهم، فأرادت الصحابة حسم مادة الفتنة، وعرض هذا الأمر على علي، والتمس منه وآثره المصريون فامتنع عليهم، وأعظم قتل عثمان وأنشأ بقول: ولو أن قومي طاوعتني سراتهم أمرتهم أمرًا بذبح الأعاديا
Discussion on the Imamate of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib. We say: Indeed 'Ali is one whose lineage and special relation to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and his upbringing by him and his marriage to his noble daughter Fatima al-Zahra - may Allah be pleased with her - are not hidden from anyone, nor his knowledge, nor his asceticism, nor his piety. As for his courage, valor, skill, and knowledge of organizing armies, leading troops, his insight into war strategies and protecting the community, these have made him a proverbial example on tongues and in hearts. It is famously narrated from him that he said: 'Verily Quraysh say that Ibn Abi Talib is a brave man, but he has no opinion in war. Allah knows! Who is more knowledgeable than me in it and more experienced? By Allah, I engaged in it before I reached twenty, and today I am nearing sixty, but there is no command for one who is not obeyed.' This is clearer than needing to prove it. Whoever doubts any of these matters is a fool for whose foolishness there is no cure. Then after the establishment of these conditions, the caliphate was contracted for him, and at that time he was the best of Allah's creation on the face of the earth and the most deserving of it. Then those who undertook to contract it for him were the senior Companions, the leaders of the people, and the best of the remaining Companions. For it is well-known that the murderers of 'Uthman - such as al-Ghafiqi, Qatana ibn Bashr al-Najibi, Suwar ibn Hamran, 'Abdullah ibn Shaddad ibn Wurqa', and 'Amr ibn al-Humq al-Khuza'i, and others - when they killed him, they intended to take control of Medina and plotted to kill its inhabitants, and they swore to the Companions that if they did not come forward to consider their situation and contract the imamate for a man among them, then the Companions wanted to cut off the source of sedition, so they presented this matter to 'Ali and asked him, and the Egyptians preferred him, but he refused them, and he magnified the murder of 'Uthman and composed saying: 'If my people had obeyed me, their leaders, I would have commanded them to slaughter the enemies.'
Source pages p. 1167

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument for the imamate of 'Ali and a defense of his caliphate. The author begins by enumerating 'Ali's well-known virtues: his lineage, his upbringing by the Prophet, his marriage to Fatima, his knowledge, asceticism, and piety. Then he focuses on his military prowess, stating that it is proverbial. He quotes 'Ali's own statement denying that he lacks military acumen, emphasizing his early and long experience. The author asserts that this is obvious and any doubter is foolish. Then he proceeds to the event after 'Uthman's murder: the caliphate was offered to 'Ali, and at that time he was the best person on earth. The author specifies that the senior Companions were the ones who contracted the caliphate for him, naming the murderers of 'Uthman to show that they were the ones pressuring for a quick decision. The Companions wanted to prevent civil strife, so they offered the caliphate to 'Ali, but he initially refused because he was appalled by 'Uthman's murder. The author ends with a verse of poetry attributed to 'Ali expressing his desire to fight the murderers. This passage defends 'Ali's rightful claim and shows that his acceptance of the caliphate was reluctant and only to prevent greater evil.

Key Terms
علي بن أبي طالب
الخلافة
الصحابة
قتلة عثمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ali eagerly sought the caliphate.
Correction: The passage shows he initially refused due to the gravity of Uthman's murder and only accepted under pressure from the Companions to prevent greater sedition.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did 'Ali initially refuse the caliphate after 'Uthman's murder?
A) He did not feel qualified.
B) He was appalled by the murder of 'Uthman.
C) He preferred to stay out of politics.
D) He thought someone else was more deserving.

Key Takeaway
The passage defends 'Ali's caliphate by combining his personal excellence with the historical fact that the senior Companions offered it to him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you been offered a position of responsibility that you felt unworthy of or reluctant to accept? How did your response compare to 'Ali's initial refusal? What does his eventual acceptance teach you about serving the community when pressed by necessity?
?
'Ali lamented, 'but there is no command for one who is not obeyed.' Have you ever experienced being in a position where you had the right insight or authority but were not listened to? How does that feel, and what can you learn from 'Ali's perseverance despite that?
?
The senior Companions offered 'Ali the caliphate because they knew he was the best. But 'Ali did not seek it. Examine your own heart: When you are qualified for something, do you wait for others to recognize you, or do you pursue it? Which attitude is more praiseworthy before Allah?

The Murder of Uthman and the First Offer to Ali
Describes the killers of Uthman and the first offer of caliphate to Ali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical context of the caliphate offer to Ali after Uthman's murder and why Ali initially refused.

Core Idea
The caliphate was offered to Ali under duress, and he refused out of reverence for Uthman.

This passage recounts the events following the assassination of Caliph Uthman. The killers threatened Medina, prompting the Companions to quickly offer the caliphate to Ali. However, Ali, horrified by the murder, declined and remained in his home. Understanding this episode is crucial for grasping the early political dynamics among the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the narrative.
Pay attention to the names of the killers and the sequence of events.
2
Identify the killers and their threat
List the named killers and note their intention to seize Medina and kill its people if a caliph was not appointed.
The killers swore an oath (hulaf) to this effect.
3
Understand the Companions' response
Recognize that the Companions acted to prevent fitna by offering the caliphate to Ali.
The Egyptians preferred Ali, but this does not mean all Companions agreed.
4
Examine Ali's refusal
Ali refused the offer, expressing horror at Uthman's murder and withdrawing to his house.
He composed a line of poetry lamenting that his people did not obey him to slay the enemies.
5
Reflect on the historical significance
Consider how this event is used in sectarian debates about the caliphate and Ali's role.
Some may wrongly assume Ali eagerly sought power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم بعد ثبوت هذه الشرائط فقد عقدت له الخلافة وهو يومئذ أفضل خليقة الله تعالى على وجه الأرض وأولاهم بها، ثم المتولي لعقدها له كبار الصحابة وأئمة الخلق وخيار من بقي من الصحابة، فإن من المشهور أن قتلة عثمان له كالغافقي وكتانة بن بشر النجيبي، وسوار بن حمران وعبد الله بن شديد بن ورقاء وعمرو بن الحمق الخزاعيين، وآخرين منهم لما قتلوه قصدوا الاستيلاء على المدينة وهموا بالفتك بأهلها وحلفوا على ذلك للصحابة متى لم يقدموا للنظر في أمرهم ويعقدوا الإمامة لرجل منهم، فأرادت الصحابة حسم مادة الفتنة، وعرض هذا الأمر على على الله، والتمس منه وآثره المصريون فامتنع عليهم، وأعظم قتل عثمان الله وأنشأ بقول: ولو أن قومي طاوعتني سراتهم أمرتهم أمرًا بذبح الأعاديا ولزم بيته
Then after these conditions were established, the caliphate was contracted for him, and he was on that day the best of Allah's creation on the face of the earth and the most worthy of it. Then those who undertook the contract for him were the senior Companions, the leaders of the creation, and the best of those remaining from the Companions. For it is well-known that the killers of Uthman, such as al-Ghafiqi, Kinana bin Bashr an-Najibi, Sawwar bin Hamran, Abdullah bin Shaddad bin Warqa', and Amr bin al-Humq al-Khuza'i, and others among them, after they killed him, intended to seize Medina and plotted to kill its people, and they swore to that against the Companions if they did not come forward to consider their matter and appoint the imamate for one of their men. So the Companions wanted to cut off the source of fitna, and they presented this matter to Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, and they requested from him, and the Egyptians preferred him, but he refused them, and he magnified the killing of Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him, and he composed saying: 'If my people's nobles had obeyed me, I would have commanded them an order to slaughter the enemies.' And he stayed in his house.
Source pages p. 1168

Commentary
This passage provides a historical account of the events immediately following the murder of the third caliph, Uthman ibn Affan. It begins by stating that after certain conditions (presumably the qualifications for leadership) were established, the caliphate was given to Ali, who was the best of Allah's creation at that time and most deserving. The ones who conducted the contract for him were the senior Companions and the best remaining. Then it describes the killers of Uthman, listing names such as al-Ghafiqi, Kinana, Sawwar, Abdullah, and Amr, and notes that they intended to seize Medina and threaten its inhabitants, swearing to harm the Companions unless they appointed a caliph from among them. To prevent fitna (discord), the Companions offered the caliphate to Ali, but he refused, expressing his horror at Uthman's murder by composing a line of poetry in which he laments that if his people had obeyed him, he would have commanded them to slay the enemies. After this, he remained in his house, indicating his withdrawal from the matter.

Key Terms

الخلافة
الصحابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ali eagerly sought the caliphate after Uthman's murder.
Correction: This passage shows Ali initially refused the offer and was horrified by Uthman's murder.

Checkpoint
What did the killers of Uthman swear to do if the Companions did not appoint a caliph?
A) Leave Medina
B) Seize Medina and kill its people
C) Submit to the Companions
D) Go to Syria

Key Takeaway
Ali's initial refusal of the caliphate demonstrates his reverence for Uthman and unwillingness to accept power under coercion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been offered a position or role that required you to overlook an injustice? Do you have the courage to refuse such an offer, even if it means losing status or opportunity? What would it take for you to 'stay in your house' like Ali did?
?
When you are confronted with a morally compromised situation, do you have the wisdom to step back, or do you rush into it thinking you can fix it from within? Ali's refusal shows restraint—where in your life do you need to exercise that same restraint today?
?
Ali expressed his grief over Uthman's murder with a line of poetry. How do you process tragedy? Do you have a way to mourn and honor what is lost without being paralyzed by it, or do you let it consume you? What would you need to change to handle loss more like Ali did?

The Refusal of Talha and Zubayr
Narrates the refusal of Talha and Zubayr to accept caliphate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reasons behind Talha and Zubayr's refusal of the caliphate as narrated by Imam al-Nasafi.

Core Idea
Their refusal was due to deep reverence, not ambition.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi continues the historical account of the caliphate after Uthman's murder. After Ali declined, the offer was made to Talha and then al-Zubayr. Their response reveals a profound sense of denial and veneration for the office, as well as the turmoil of the times.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Note the key phrases and the poetic verse.
The verse by Talha is a personal lament.
2
Identify the key figures
Notice that Talha and Zubayr are offered the caliphate, and both refuse. The Basrans preferred Talha, but he still refused.
3
Understand the reason for refusal
The text concludes that their refusal was out of 'inkar' (denial) and 'i'zam' (veneration). Reflect on what this means.
This indicates their humility and the gravity of the situation.
4
Analyze the historical context
Consider the turmoil after Uthman's killing. Why might Talha and Zubayr feel unable to take the caliphate?
Their refusal underscores the chaotic nature of the time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم عرض ذلك على طلحة وآثره البصريون، فأبى ذلك وكرهه وأنشأ يقول: ومن عجب الأيام والدهر أنني بقيت وحيدًا لا أمر ولا أحلى لقتل عثمان ثم عرض على الزبير فامتنع أيضا كل ذلك إنكارا منهم وإعظاما
Then this was presented to Talha, and the Basrans preferred him, but he refused and disliked it and composed saying: 'And among the wonders of days and time is that I remain alone, I command not and I rule not, for the killing of Uthman.' Then it was presented to al-Zubayr, but he also refrained, all of that out of denial and veneration from them.
Source pages p. 1169

Commentary
This passage continues the narrative of the search for a caliph. After Ali's refusal, the matter was presented to Talha. The Basrans (the party from Basra) preferred him, but Talha refused and disliked the offer. He composed a verse expressing his astonishment that he remained alone (without authority) and that he neither commands nor rules in the aftermath of Uthman's killing. Then the offer was made to al-Zubayr, who also refrained. The author notes that all these refusals were out of denial (inkar) of the situation and veneration (i'zam) for the caliphate, meaning they did not feel worthy or found the circumstances too distressing.

Key Terms
طلحة
الزبير
إنكار
إعظام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Talha and Zubayr desired power and were ambitious for the caliphate.
Correction: Their refusal shows that they were motivated by denial of the situation and veneration for the office, not ambition.

Checkpoint
Why did Talha and Zubayr refuse the caliphate according to this passage?
A) They were afraid of the killers
B) They did not consider themselves qualified
C) Out of denial and veneration
D) They wanted to support Ali

Key Takeaway
Talha and Zubayr's refusal of the caliphate was not from cowardice but from deep respect and denial of being fit for the role in such turbulent times.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are offered a position of honor or leadership, does your heart immediately leap at the opportunity, or do you hesitate with the same denial and veneration these companions showed? What would it take for you to say, like Talha, 'I remain alone, I command not and I rule not'?
?
Is there a role or responsibility in your life that you have accepted out of ambition rather than out of genuine humility? How can you recalibrate your intentions to reflect the reverence that kept Talha and Zubayr from grasping power?
?
If you were to face a situation where you feel unworthy of a task (like Talha felt unworthy of the caliphate), would you still take it on out of ego, or would you have the courage to step back? What is one area where you need to admit your unworthiness and trust Allah's plan instead?

Ali's Reluctant Acceptance and the Pledge
Describes pressure on Ali to accept caliphate and the pledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Ali accepted the caliphate only after immense pressure from the leading Companions and for the preservation of the community, and that his acceptance was reluctant and based on public interest.

Core Idea
Ali accepted the caliphate under duress, for the common good.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabṣirat al-Adilla concludes the account of Ali's rise to the caliphate. It emphasizes that Ali did not seek power but was compelled by the leading Muhajirun and Ansar, who feared the spread of fitna. Their pleas and Ali's eventual acceptance highlight the gravity of the moment and the maturity of the early Muslim community's decision-making.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice the strong language used by the companions, such as 'for the sake of Allah and His curse'.
The passage contains both narrative and a list of notables.
2
Identify the companions' motives
Determine why the Muhajirun and Ansar pressured Ali. Look for phrases like 'to preserve the remainder of the trust' and 'to protect the abode of the Hijra'.
Their fear of fitna (discord) is the driving force.
3
Examine Ali's hesitation
Notice that Ali accepted 'after hardship' and only when he saw it as beneficial. Ask yourself why he was reluctant.
Ali knew he was the most knowledgeable and best, but still hesitated.
4
List the pledgers
Identify the six Companions specifically named as giving allegiance. They include Khuzayma bin Thabit, Abu al-Haytham, Muhammad bin Maslama, Ammar, Abu Musa, and Abdullah bin Abbas.
The passage says 'and many others' indicating broader support.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلما حلف أهل الفتنة على الفتك بأهل المدينة والقاح الفتنة بها اجتمع وجوه المهاجرين والأنصار - رضي الله عنهم - من عشية اليوم الثالث - على ما روي - من قتل عثمان فسألوا عليا لله ولعنه هذا الأمر وأقسموا عليه فيه، وناشدوه الله في حفظ بقية الأمانة وصيانة دار الهجرة، فدخل في ذلك بعد شدة وبعد أن رأه مصلحة ورأى القوم ذلك بعلمهم وعلمه أنه أعلم من بقى من الصحابة وأفضلهم وأولاهم به فمد يده، وبايعه جماعة ممن حضر منهم: خزيمة بن ثابت، وأبو الهيثم بن التيهان ومحمد بن مسلمة، وعمار وأبو موسى الأشعري، وعبد الله بن عباس - رضي الله عنهم - في رجال يكثر عددهم
When the people of fitna swore to kill the people of Medina and to incite fitna therein, the leaders of the Muhajirun and Ansar - may Allah be pleased with them - gathered on the evening of the third day - as is narrated - from the killing of Uthman, and they asked Ali, for the sake of Allah and His curse, for this matter, and they swore to him concerning it, and they adjured him by Allah to preserve the remainder of the trust and to protect the abode of the Hijra. So he entered into it after hardship and after he saw it as a benefit, and the people saw that with their knowledge, and he knew that he was the most knowledgeable of those remaining among the Companions, the best, and the most worthy of it. So he extended his hand, and a group of those present gave him allegiance, among them: Khuzayma bin Thabit, Abu al-Haytham bin al-Tayyihan, Muhammad bin Maslama, Ammar, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and Abdullah bin Abbas - may Allah be pleased with them - and many others.
Source pages p. 1169

Commentary
This passage concludes the narrative of Ali's acceptance of the caliphate. It states that when the people of fitna (the killers and their supporters) swore to kill the inhabitants of Medina and spread discord, the leading Muhajirun and Ansar gathered on the evening of the third day after Uthman's murder. They asked Ali, adjuring him by Allah and using strong language ('for the sake of Allah and His curse'), to accept the caliphate, and they swore to him. They beseeched him to preserve the remaining trust (the Muslim community) and protect the city of the Hijra (Medina). Ali agreed after difficulty, and only after he saw it as a beneficial move. The community recognized his knowledge and virtue; he knew he was the most knowledgeable, best, and most deserving of those remaining. He then extended his hand (the gesture of accepting allegiance), and a group gave him the bay'a (pledge). The author lists notable Companions who pledged: Khuzayma bin Thabit, Abu al-Haytham bin al-Tayyihan, Muhammad bin Maslama, Ammar (bin Yasir), Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and Abdullah bin Abbas, along with many others.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Ali was eager to become caliph.
Correction: This passage shows he accepted only under pressure and for public benefit, not personal ambition.

Checkpoint

A) Khuzayma bin Thabit
B) Abu al-Haytham bin al-Tayyihan
C) Umar ibn al-Khattab
D) Abdullah ibn Abbas

Key Takeaway
Ali accepted the caliphate reluctantly, driven by the urgent need to prevent fitna and preserve the community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you reluctantly accepted a responsibility you didn't want, simply because you saw it was necessary for the good of others? What did that experience reveal about your character?
?
Ali was the most knowledgeable and best suited, yet he hesitated. In what areas of your life are you holding back from stepping into a role you are qualified for, and what is stopping you from taking that step?
?
The companions used urgent language to call Ali to duty. Who in your life speaks to you with such urgency about your responsibilities? Do you tend to listen or to dismiss them? How can you become more receptive to such calls?

Sects and Disagreements
